  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_76e2b522-e2c2-46bf-94ac-2a8ee40de4b0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2374505045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10634920159715657603"><i>“Jesus, are all vampires over two hundred perverts?"<br/>"I am over two hundred," Jean-Claude said.<br/>"I rest my case.” </i><br/><br/>I postponed writing this review for as long as I could. Then I postponed it again. Then again. Finally I realized I need to do it right now before I forget what is was about. The reason was I have no clue how to rate the book. I was hoping for a bright idea, a Eureka! moment, something. Nothing came. And here I am as clueless as I was right after finishing. <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528158312i/25656892.jpg' width='300' height='300' alt='Clueless' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So about the plot of Circus </span>
  <span id="freeText10634920159715657603" style="display:none"><i>“Jesus, are all vampires over two hundred perverts?"<br>"I am over two hundred," Jean-Claude said.<br>"I rest my case.” </i><br><br>I postponed writing this review for as long as I could. Then I postponed it again. Then again. Finally I realized I need to do it right now before I forget what is was about. The reason was I have no clue how to rate the book. I was hoping for a bright idea, a Eureka! moment, something. Nothing came. And here I am as clueless as I was right after finishing. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528158312i/25656892.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="Clueless" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So about the plot of Circus of the Damned aka Too Many Master Vampires. A current Master Vampire of Anita's St. Louis was perceived to be weak by his peers. This means there are plenty of other undead bloodsuckers that would love nothing more than to take his place. What do you know, these Hollywood glorified monsters behave exactly like organized crime dividing the sphere of influence. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528157281i/25656831._SX540_.jpg" alt="Turf War" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>How do you challenge a Master Vampire? You move into his turf and start slaughtering <s>sheep</s> I mean those same people that decided it is possible to live side by side with creatures whose primary diet consists of human blood. As soon as slaughter started Anita realized the Master Vampire wannabe needs to be stopped. What she has not realized that others would soon follow. She also has not realized the current Master did not care much about the developing situation. Her life seemed to become full of excitement with people around being killed left and right in the most gruesome ways. <br><br>I already mentioned I have no clue about the rating: 3 or 4 stars? On one hand Anita's wisecracks are great and remind me of Kate Daniels in the first books (she - Kate - refined the noble art of wisecracking later in the series). <br><br><i>"He's dead, Richard, a walking corpse. It doesn't matter how pretty he is, or how compelling, he's still dead. I don't date corpses. A girl's got to have some standards."</i><br>Critics did not like this bit too much: they got offended thinking Anita's dating preferences showed her racism towards poor creatures of the night. Personally, I liked her attitude.<br><br>At times I even cared for her. Also nobody can accuse the plot of dragging. There was enough action to fill almost 300 pages (my edition). <br><br>On the other hand Anita is not the brightest girl on the block, no matter what she thinks about herself. Some of the characters desperately wanted to become fully fledged 3-D depiction of real people, but failed. <br><br>3 stars, or 4 stars? I just don't know. Can anybody help? The current rating is a placeholder by the way - a subject to change. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528156990i/25656770._SX540_.jpg" alt="Puzzled" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Update June 5 2018. I decided upon the rating: 4 stars. I rated Dresden Files #3 the same and it was weaker.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10634920159715657603" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_87183234" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87183234" />
    <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction"><img alt="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605816027p2/2905339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87183234?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction">Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87183234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9282651835239523641">I am really enjoying my rereading of this series. Going back to the beginning of the series has reminded me why I continue to read along even though it has morphed into another beast entirely. These early books were so great because the men and the sex weren’t the focus of the entire freaking plot.<br/><br/>Here Anita is still working as an animator and an assistant to preternatural police force. Anita has a full plate, as usual, after a full night of corpse raising, she’s then hounded by members of “the </span>
  <span id="freeText9282651835239523641" style="display:none">I am really enjoying my rereading of this series. Going back to the beginning of the series has reminded me why I continue to read along even though it has morphed into another beast entirely. These early books were so great because the men and the sex weren’t the focus of the entire freaking plot.<br /><br />Here Anita is still working as an animator and an assistant to preternatural police force. Anita has a full plate, as usual, after a full night of corpse raising, she’s then hounded by members of “the vamp hater Church or somesuch” to give up the resting place of the Master of the City (Jean Claude), then a body turns up drained by what appears to be a rogue pack of vamps which leads her to The Circus of the Damned and into close proximity with vampire Jean Claude, a sexy vampire she’d rather avoid. He’s been trying to make her his human servant but she stubbornly refuses, even when it means putting her own life in jeopardy. There’s a whole lot of that “Ma petite I have marked you, you are mine” “I kill vampires, I don’t serve them” nonsense going on. She must train an apprentice animator, face down an angry lamia, crazed humans, out of control zombies and deal with a dangerous master vampire. It sounds exhausting but I have to hand it to Hamilton because I was never lost. We’re also introduced to Richard when he was still sweet and sexy and not quite so angry and rigid as he appears in the later novels..<br /><br />Once again there is way too much focus on clothing (who cares) and the gun descriptions (snore). Personally, I am still not dying to discover what color Anita’s Nike swishes will be every other page and if the match her t shirt. I already know that she is not a girly-girl because it’s mentioned over and over. We all know Jean Claude has a preference for lacy floofy blouses and his own nipples. Do we need to be constantly reminded of this? It’s a little painful to read this stuff the second time around but the quick pacing and intriguing characters carry the book for me and I enjoyed the many plotlines here, none of which focus on sex I might add.<br /><br />Despite a lame-ass villain and too much arguing from Anita, I enjoyed this as much as the previous two in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9282651835239523641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13339729211400169451" style="display:none"><b> Anita Blake to the rescue again???!!!<br><br>I'm afraid my love affair with Anita's badass ways may be coming to an end. I'm starting to question if you are capable of love.<br><br>Actually, Anita really pissed me off with her betrayal in this episode. I need for her to develop some level of softness. <div id="review_327129851" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/327129851" />
    <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light"><img alt="Crystal Starr Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573066911p2/3990525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/327129851?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Starr Light" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780143144038" href="/book/show/6399685-circus-of-the-damned">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=hello-my-name-is-mary-sue">hello-my-name-is-mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=fashion-accident">fashion-accident</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer327129851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2000846145818103956">"Your questions will make something simple last all...day." <br/><br/>Just three books in, and already we can see a pattern forming. Dudes come to Anita to have her do something; she says, in no uncertain terms, "No". Dolph calls her to investigate a murder; it ends up being the weirdest, most unusual murder Anita has ever seen. Jean-Claude makes the moves on her; Anita tells him to F@#$ off. Anita does minor investigating, bad guys come out of the woodworks to try to kill her, Anita is rude and sarcastic</span>
  <span id="freeText2000846145818103956" style="display:none">"Your questions will make something simple last all...day." <br /><br />Just three books in, and already we can see a pattern forming. Dudes come to Anita to have her do something; she says, in no uncertain terms, "No". Dolph calls her to investigate a murder; it ends up being the weirdest, most unusual murder Anita has ever seen. Jean-Claude makes the moves on her; Anita tells him to F@#$ off. Anita does minor investigating, bad guys come out of the woodworks to try to kill her, Anita is rude and sarcastic to a bunch of people, and suddenly Anita is fighting off the Most Powerful *FILL*IN*THE*BLANK*.<br /><br />This book is no different. Some Human First members want Anita to rat out Jean-Claude; she refuses. She is called to a murder scene; the victim has been bitten to death by 5 or more vampires. Back to Jean-Claude where she and he fight like cats and dogs. FIGHT SCENE! Then Anita is racing off to her "night job". FIGHT SCENE! Bad guys try to kill her, Anita stumbles onto some new vampires, and before you know it, the city is about to be turned upside down by a 1million year old vampire--the oldest EVAH.<br /><br />I'm rather torn about this book. There are actually things I like. Anita values her independence and free will and does NOT like Jean-Claude's stalker-ish behavior. The book is pretty fast-paced, and if you don't go in expecting Anita to do much investigating (pretty much everything just falls into her lap--how nice!), it's pretty exciting. It's also nice to have some action scenes, instead of many, many kissy-kissy scenes we see in vampire books. And, oddly enough, I actually LIKED Richard and Anita's cute meet (though I have heard tons about how THAT ends up...and it makes me sad :( ).<br /><br />But there are oh, so many things that drives me nuts about these books.<br /><br />1. Anita Blake. God, this is an unlikable woman! I can only take so much of this, "I am better than everyone else, even though I am ONLY 24 years old and have been in the business a whopping THREE years". Half the time, she sounds like a petulant child, bragging about how many toys (guns) she has and how well she can use them or telling someone to f@#$ off (and she does the latter A LOT). Or playing p!ssing games with the police (who should be fired for all the sexual harassment!). The other half of the time, she sounds like a 40 year old woman, coaching someone who is ONLY FOUR YEARS YOUNGER THAN HER and calling him "kiddo".<br /><br />2. Action Scenes. Is it possible to have too many? When you forget what was going on and what the plot was, yes. This happened to me frequently. Why the big fight at Circus of the Damned with the Snake? Why did the vampires reveal themselves to Anita (when she had NO IDEA who they were before) at the cemetery with Larry? Why was Anita so easily duped into driving an hour into the boonies only to be chased into a cave where the vamps try to kill her? Isn't this supposed to be Anita, the most awesome, kick-@ss Vampire Hunter in the Mid-West?<br /><br />3. Clothing. Every person has to have a run-down of what they are wearing. And not just once; no, we have to know what EVERYONE is wearing at any time. So when Anita changes, you hear about it. When Jean-Claude is on the scene, expect at least a paragraph or two on his frilly shirt.<br /><br />4. CTRL+C -&gt; CTRL+P. New "characters" have nearly the same description as old ones. St. Louis must have the highest population of beefy, muscular men who lift weights, because, I swear, it seemed not a page went by before Anita mentioned how muscular so-and-so was and how he must lift weights.<br /><br />5. TMI. In case you were ever curious what exercise routine Anita and Ronnie do when they hit the gym, don't worry. LKH will let you know what machines they start at, who is best at what (Anita is better at arms, Ronnie with legs), and when they do cardio. Just what I open a Vampire novel to read. NOT.<br /><br />6. Super-powered villains. For once, couldn't Anita just defeat a troup of vampires, instead of a showdown between her and the Most Awesome, 1 Million Year Old Vampire? What about a voodoo practitioner instead of The Best Voodoo Practitioner in Missouri? I have no idea how all these super powered beings keep coming to St. Louis (not the biggest city in the US) and just throw themselves in front of Anita's Browning.<br /><br />Okay, so that was a lot of complaining. This book wasn't horrible. It was okay, it's just that after reading three Anita books in a row, I'm burned out. I think I need a break before I attempt to tackle Book 4 (if I want to at all--I am beginning to think this series is just not my cup of tea). Certainly not the worst out there, but I've read better too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2000846145818103956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17395597447062244577">Without a doubt, better than the first two. I really like Jean-Claud. He is the reason I am reading these books. I have never wanted a bad guy to get the girl before, it's fun. Anita was a bit disappointing. I'm beginning to wonder if Jean-Claud deserves better.<br/><br/>The swearing is excessive and redundant. And I realize that in a series you have to make each book a stand alone and therefore have to explain the same thing several times. But does it have to be word for word? There are literally paragra</span>
  <span id="freeText17395597447062244577" style="display:none">Without a doubt, better than the first two. I really like Jean-Claud. He is the reason I am reading these books. I have never wanted a bad guy to get the girl before, it's fun. Anita was a bit disappointing. I'm beginning to wonder if Jean-Claud deserves better.<br /><br />The swearing is excessive and redundant. And I realize that in a series you have to make each book a stand alone and therefore have to explain the same thing several times. But does it have to be word for word? There are literally paragraphs that are cut and pasted into each book. Would it be too much to ask for at least new wording.... a new angle on the info?? Something!</span>

<div id="review_228033020" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228033020" />
    <a title="Tilly Slaton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6289182-tilly-slaton"><img alt="Tilly Slaton" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228033020?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tilly Slaton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tilly Slaton" href="/user/show/6289182-tilly-slaton">Tilly Slaton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6289182-tilly-slaton?shelf=reviews-completed">reviews-completed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228033020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18231786062438449308">I love Laurell Hamilton’s work. The Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter series is outstanding!<br/> <br/>The first two books in this series, Guilty Pleasures and The Laughing Corpse are amazing pieces of work.<br/> <br/>This book declares no less awesomeness. This is the book that wraps you around the series and pulls everything together. This book is really the beginning of the journey that whips and turns you into a reality that is completely twisted, morbid and simply put, cool!<br/> <br/>Anita Blake is introduced to a few charac</span>
  <span id="freeText18231786062438449308" style="display:none">I love Laurell Hamilton’s work. The Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter series is outstanding!<br /> <br />The first two books in this series, Guilty Pleasures and The Laughing Corpse are amazing pieces of work.<br /> <br />This book declares no less awesomeness. This is the book that wraps you around the series and pulls everything together. This book is really the beginning of the journey that whips and turns you into a reality that is completely twisted, morbid and simply put, cool!<br /> <br />Anita Blake is introduced to a few characters that you will no doubt adore and look forward to reading about in the future.<br /> <br />Being yanked from one Master to another, Anita is faced with a choice. A choice to betray those she is running from or a choice to try to save the humans from the monsters. Tough choice right?<br /> <br />Jean-Claude is relentless in his desires and efforts to seduce the one woman who has the power that once bound to his, will make him even more incredibly strong and deadly.<br /> <br />A new character is brought to life, Richard Zeeman. His charming smile and human body draws Anita into a chance to live a normal life. Well, as normal as raising zombies and hunting and ripping hearts out of vampires. Unfortunately, she is was deceived by the very monsters she avoided.<br /> <br />Instead of trusting her instincts, Anita tip toes across the lines she carefully placed in life. The line has wavered since the second book. In this book, she considers that not all monsters are evil. She wonders if Jean-Claude is a monster. Sure, he is the walking dead. But could she love him?<br /> <br />Thrilling battles ending in death and blood shed, Anita chooses which side of monsters to fight beside. The interesting whoas in this book are grin worthy!<br /> <br />Fighting against a vampire that is over a million years old (that is the only mark in this book that is a little ridiculous in my opinion), and the servants that betray each other, the relationships become unpredictable. It was a pleasant surprise, to find myself smiling as the scenes hit me from the blind side.<br /> <br />As the other two books, I would recommend this book to anyone that is interested in paranormal (or what seems to be science fiction? weird..) worlds centered around blood and guts with a pinch of lust.<br /> <br />I would strongly suggest that this book not be read by children or immature young adults.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18231786062438449308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_46147083" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46147083" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/205934-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592372937p2/205934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46147083?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/205934-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46147083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5990197008711644994"><p>For all the Anita Blake books - I started this series with my then friend, Meredith - she actually got me hooked that fateful summer of 2000 when I was living on her wooden floor in Brooklyn. We were both unemployed and bored and got hooked into this series. I loved Anita Blake because it was before I discovered the new genre - what I like to call "badass chicks who kick ass!" written in first person - and so she was all empowering and of course there were hot vampires and werewolves in it.</p><p> Unfo</p></span>
  <span id="freeText5990197008711644994" style="display:none"><p>For all the Anita Blake books - I started this series with my then friend, Meredith - she actually got me hooked that fateful summer of 2000 when I was living on her wooden floor in Brooklyn. We were both unemployed and bored and got hooked into this series. I loved Anita Blake because it was before I discovered the new genre - what I like to call "badass chicks who kick ass!" written in first person - and so she was all empowering and of course there were hot vampires and werewolves in it.</p><p> Unfortunately, Laurell K Hamilton doesn't have much taste in the way of clothing and mood...and sometimes I think she "tells" too much instead of "shows." I also think that somewhere down the line the editors decided to just give her cart blanche because she most definitely has cut and paste some paragraphs here and there from one book to another.</p><p> The other thing I find annoying is that Anita likes to pick fights for no reason and seems to have the little dog syndrome - always barking up at the big guns. And for some reason as the series goes on, the more sexual it gets and also the more ridiculous it gets. She has some interesting elements and some interesting characters and definitely isn't afraid to be violent - which I love. But then I got annoyed and moved on to other authors who still work with their editors!!! Needless to say, I stopped reading the series after Incubus Dreams. My fav of the series is Obsidian Butterfly. It has the least "retelling" and show boating.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="5990197008711644994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3965501" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11230229000326587685">I also thought the premise of Anita Blake was pretty cool. She's an Animator, see? She raises zombies for a living. And vampires are legal citizens. Eventually, she's supposed to get involved with both a vampire and a werewolf. I say eventually cause even though I thought this was a central theme of the books, I've read 2 and a half of them and there have been nary a creature-of-the-night and vampire hunter smoochie. I take that back. There was one, but it was one of those contrived "fake kiss s</span>
  <span id="freeText11230229000326587685" style="display:none">I also thought the premise of Anita Blake was pretty cool. She's an Animator, see? She raises zombies for a living. And vampires are legal citizens. Eventually, she's supposed to get involved with both a vampire and a werewolf. I say eventually cause even though I thought this was a central theme of the books, I've read 2 and a half of them and there have been nary a creature-of-the-night and vampire hunter smoochie. I take that back. There was one, but it was one of those contrived "fake kiss so the cops think we're just a couple, but ooo, did you feel the attraction anyway" snogs.<br /><br />And I am over both the Sweet Valley Syndrome* and the Too Cool for School Because I Am NOT GIRLY, Dammit themes. Yeah, yeah, Anita, you had to go buy a dress to sneak into the vampire freak party because you are Not Girly and therefore did not own a black dress. Fine, fine, that pink shirt in your closet must have been a gift because "the thought that I had actually spent money on anything pink was more than I could bear." And the whole making fun of wedding dresses and bridesmaids' dresses? Yes, we know, Anita. Stop rolling your eyes so damned much, we get that you are NOT GIRLY. Over it.<br /><br />* Yes, I read Sweet Valley Twins and Sweet Valley High books once upon a time. And though the books are a series, each one is written so that if it's your first foray into Sweet Valley, you get the paragraph description of how the girls are a perfect size 6 and they have matching gold lavalieres and Jessica is the wild one and Elizabeth is the book worm, yadda, yadda, yadda. </span>

<div id="review_495368870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Kami" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12185626-kami"><img alt="Kami" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/495368870?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kami" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kami" href="/user/show/12185626-kami">Kami</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer495368870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2878152027527581763">Absolutely hated the book. Maybe it's a case of reading too many in the series so close together but I am so done with the love/hate thing Anita has with Jean-Claude and her supposed badass attitude. The writing misses the mark trying to create what I would consider a strong dominant character and instead the character comes across as very insecure, hates herself and everyone around her and has a really lousy sense of fashion. Maybe others like that kind of psychological baggage but it's not for</span>
  <span id="freeText2878152027527581763" style="display:none">Absolutely hated the book. Maybe it's a case of reading too many in the series so close together but I am so done with the love/hate thing Anita has with Jean-Claude and her supposed badass attitude. The writing misses the mark trying to create what I would consider a strong dominant character and instead the character comes across as very insecure, hates herself and everyone around her and has a really lousy sense of fashion. Maybe others like that kind of psychological baggage but it's not for me. If Anita truly hated Jean-Claude that much then why does she keep going back when she needs his talents and then hates him for it. Why would Jean-Claude keep going back to Anita? It's like there should be some history between them that has fostered Anita's hostility towards Jean-Claude but I'm tired of waiting for it to come out if it ever does. The storyline has become way too predictable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2878152027527581763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1528195790" />
    <a title="Alen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10259320-alen"><img alt="Alen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586344821p2/10259320.jpg" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1528195790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8667446142046714737">Circus of the Damned did not scare me or grossed me out as much as Guilty Pleasures or The Laughing Corpse. I also didn't like it as much as the last two books of the series.<br/><br/>Jean-Claude is turning Anita's life into one hell of a big mess; Anita is firstly baited by a vampire Master called Alejandro, who controls a pack of rabid vampires who have chewing up people and leaving them on the cemetery. Alejandro wishes to know who is the Vampire Master controlling the city of St.Louis, and his where h</span>
  <span id="freeText8667446142046714737" style="display:none">Circus of the Damned did not scare me or grossed me out as much as Guilty Pleasures or The Laughing Corpse. I also didn't like it as much as the last two books of the series.<br><br>Jean-Claude is turning Anita's life into one hell of a big mess; Anita is firstly baited by a vampire Master called Alejandro, who controls a pack of rabid vampires who have chewing up people and leaving them on the cemetery. Alejandro wishes to know who is the Vampire Master controlling the city of St.Louis, and his where he rests daily. <br>Secondly, there's a pre-historical vampire master, who is millions of years old, a miniature of a man, with a monkey-like face called Oliver. He also wants to know who the vampire master of the city is.<br>Anita is aware that she and Jean-Claude are both lusting for each other, but she tries not to get that lust get in the way - I have to say that I admire her resistance, she isn't even tempted with immortality or super strength, which she can have, if she only allows Jean-Claude to give two more marks to complete the human-slave/vampire master bond.<br><br>Reasons why I didn't like Circus of the Damned as much as the two last books:<br><br>- less action-packed;<br>- a lot of characters getting on my nerves.<br><br>I'm still really intrigued by Edward, I was happy to see him again, even if the circumstances weren't the best, but hey, we're talking about Edward right? If Edward is around it means that shit is about to get down. <br>Still, the drama between Anita and Jean-Claude is beginning to be infuriating.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385177889ra/7089410.gif" width="245" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jean-Claude is always determined to seduce her, and she is stubborn as usual. I hope that after this book they either end up ripping each others' clothes off or simply ending their flirting, and they continue their paths separately. I believe I won't be able to handle this on and off thing anymore.<br><br>Larry is a new character who is introduced in this book, furthermore, he was also the one who peeved me the most. He is a new animator, he hasn't even finish college, and he certainly has never had a brush with death before. Larry's experience with vampire hunting, raising zombies from their graves is zero, the lad is as innocent as they come, not good for the kind of job he has, and definitely not good in terms of survival. If I were Anita I would've slapped him a couple of times, Larry really got on my nerves, as all he was good for was being a distraction. Helpless as a lamb.<br><br>Despite not having liked Circus if the Damned as much as the previous books, I still loved it so very much. I'll have to keep on reading xD<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401075391ra/9753666.gif" width="500" height="279" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="8667446142046714737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText11915567923834627311" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br />A band of rogue masters has come to town and are out in the streets killing people. Anita Blake will have to decide who she is loyal to in this action packed, fast paced novel.<br /><br />I reread this book, and while I remembered quite a few of the plot points, I still enjoyed the book. Anita Blake is still a kick butt necromancer who happens to execute vampires along with helping the police regional preternatural crimes unit. With all of this going on she still finds time to date, which is the one aspect of this book that I do not like. Richard makes numerous comments about her line of work and how it is unsafe and I feel as a character Anita would have acted differently than she does and would not have put up with it.<br /><br />Other than that this book was a fun reread and I enjoyed being back in this world.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15433435185413612288">Amazing book, every scene was a pretzel of details wound up in a spring of potential energy that was soon to be released. The viewpoints expressed established a world I am not sure I want to travel as it may damage my ideas of right and wrong beyond any chance of redemption.</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer112956887&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112956887" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9027702736651096467">Okay Anita, I admire that her character is hardcore, strong, independent, but I think she goes a little overboard in describing how tough she is. Okay, we get it, you are almost a man in a woman's body. No wait, you're better than a man in a woman's body. <br/><br/>It's amazing to me how she never seems to get any sleep because she keeps getting into trouble every three hours. How can you walk around with no sleep and still fight the bad guys. Speaking of bad guys, how is it that no matter how much troubl</span>
  <span id="freeText9027702736651096467" style="display:none">Okay Anita, I admire that her character is hardcore, strong, independent, but I think she goes a little overboard in describing how tough she is. Okay, we get it, you are almost a man in a woman's body. No wait, you're better than a man in a woman's body. <br /><br />It's amazing to me how she never seems to get any sleep because she keeps getting into trouble every three hours. How can you walk around with no sleep and still fight the bad guys. Speaking of bad guys, how is it that no matter how much trouble she's in, she always find someway to get out, whether she's shot, stabbed, bleeding to death, broken arm, ten vampires coming at her at once and yet somehow she survives and manages to make sarcastic comments along the way. <br /><br />Now as for Jean Claude...I seriously despise the way she treats him. We all know you really do like the vampire, and the guy hasn't done anything that's so bad to her that she has to be so bitchy to him all the time. Sometimes during simple conversations with him she's just rude and nasty to the guy and that is what I don't like. I don't know how Jean Claude can continue to love her, especially when she betrayed him in this novel just because she didn't want to become his human slave. She actually tried to get him killed. Who needs a woman like that? And Jean Claude just takes it all in stride and still chases after the woman who claims to hate him so much. <br /><br />Circus of the Damned is the best book I've read as far as action and the mention of Jean Claude. I love the different vampires and the snake woman. Pretty darn cool. Oh and her description of Richard when she first met him, naked in a bed surrounded by vampires and lycans was unbelievably sexy. Although I often wondered what the hell was he doing? That was never explain, my only guess is that he turned into a wolf and was sleeping off the affects when Anita came into the room. </span>

<div id="review_1864520010" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1864520010" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5838986-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466996530p2/5838986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1864520010?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/5838986-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1864520010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7542596756961573958">I'm tapping out. I can't understand how anyone could be motivated enough to continue this series. This book reinforces all the things that bugged me about the first two and manages to drum up some new irks at the same time. <br/><br/>Anita is awful. I long for the day when authors can write independent, strong women without making them into raging assholes. I checked myself and thought whether or not her behavior would be more acceptable if she were a man, but no. Insulting others is not a form of wit. It</span>
  <span id="freeText7542596756961573958" style="display:none">I'm tapping out. I can't understand how anyone could be motivated enough to continue this series. This book reinforces all the things that bugged me about the first two and manages to drum up some new irks at the same time. <br /><br />Anita is awful. I long for the day when authors can write independent, strong women without making them into raging assholes. I checked myself and thought whether or not her behavior would be more acceptable if she were a man, but no. Insulting others is not a form of wit. It doesn't matter if you feel a twinge of guilt afterward; no matter how much you feel you need to prove yourself, you don't have to belittle others. Constantly mentioning how skilled you are, how many guns you have, and stressing that anything pink or dressy is disgusting to you is annoying to me and <i>not</i> proof that you're strong. If you hate pink, you hate pink (I do), but consistently distancing yourself from anything remotely girly seems a bit much. It comes across as insecure. <br /><br />When you can't root for the main character, the plot is fill-in-the-blank, and the writing isn't as witty as it tries to be, there's no point in reading. I was really hoping I'd like this series (20+ published books sounds amazing), but I won't be going on.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7542596756961573958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('k8PiUB6c9ykV+HH5HDPZDYTBtr1d+OZpstNo8vx7sS5mQpiMf6IVQfT+ucDVeJzRRdITzI8adKXijNqr0hlcAw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lSDhCXrg8LOF6p39Lwy0OiETHSfaL0C+yrRbc5g7/N5goZvVG94S22TsVcTmR/Hm4AC4VgjN0nKa6+kqtlkR8w==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText9470500510688997539" style="display:none">Laurell K. Hamilton is one of the leading writers of paranormal fiction. A #1 New York Times bestselling author, Hamilton writes the popular Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter novels and the Meredith Gentry series. She is also the creator of a bestselling comic book series based on her Anita Blake novels and published by Marvel Comics. Hamilton is a full-time writer and lives in the suburbs of St. Louis with her family.</span>

The investigation leads her to Cerulean Sins, a vampire-run establishment that deals in erotic videos, videos that cater to very specific tastes. Anita knows one creature of the night who has such interests — Jean-Claude’s visitor. But if Anita brings Musette down, the repercussions could cost her everything she holds dear.\n\nOnce a sworn enemy of all monsters, Anita is now the human consort of both Master Vampire Jean Claude and leopard shapeshifter Micah. When a centuries-old vampire hits St. Louis, Anita finds herself needing all the dark forces her passion can muster to save the ones she loves.\n\nAnita Blake returns to find hell hath no fury like a
